[Operator Instructions] I'd like to now turn the call over to Mike. Michael Creedon

Thanks, Bob. Good morning, everyone, and thank you for joining our call today. Today is a very exciting day for our company. As I'm sure most of you saw this morning, we announced that Brigade-Macellum will acquire our Family Dollar business for a total price of just over $1 billion. After a thorough review of our strategic alternatives, the company determined that a sale of Family Dollar is the best way to achieve our value creation goals. Dollar Tree and Family Dollar are two different businesses with limited synergies, and each is at a very different stage of its journey. Separating them will enable each banner to be led and managed by a dedicated team that can focus exclusively on that banner's distinct needs and on realizing each banner's full potential. Separating will also enable investors to own a business they value more without also having to own a business they value less or that may not fit in their investment profile. It should also make it easier for the market to properly value each business. Under the terms of the deal, subject to certain closing adjustments, Dollar Tree will receive just over $800 million in cash proceeds. The deal should close in about 90 days, and Family Dollar will remain headquartered here in Chesapeake. ê° ë¸Œëœë“œë¥¼ ë¶„ë¦¬í•¨ìœ¼ë¡œì¨ ê°ê°ì˜ ë¸Œëœë“œê°€ ë…íŠ¹í•œ ìš”êµ¬ì‚¬í•­ì— ì§‘ì¤‘í•˜ê³  ì „ì²´ ì ì¬ë ¥ì„ ì‹¤í˜„í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë„ë¡ ì „ë‹´ íŒ€ì´ ì´ëŒê³  ê´€ë¦¬í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆê²Œ ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë˜í•œ, ë¶„ë¦¬ë¥¼ í†µí•´ íˆ¬ììë“¤ì€ ìì‹ ì´ ëœ ê°€ì¹˜ ìˆë‹¤ê³  ì—¬ê¸°ëŠ” ì‚¬ì—…ì„ ì†Œìœ í•˜ì§€ ì•Šê³ ë„, ë” ê°€ì¹˜ ìˆê²Œ í‰ê°€í•˜ëŠ” ì‚¬ì—…ì—ë§Œ íˆ¬ìí•  ìˆ˜ ìˆê²Œ ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì´ëŠ” ì‹œì¥ì´ ê° ì‚¬ì—…ì„ ì ì ˆíˆ í‰ê°€í•˜ëŠ” ë°ì—ë„ ë„ì›€ì´ ë  ê²ƒì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê±°ë˜ ì¡°ê±´ì— ë”°ë¼, ì¼ì •í•œ ë§ˆê° ì¡°ì •ì„ ê±°ì³, ë‹¬ëŸ¬ íŠ¸ë¦¬ëŠ” 8ì–µ ë‹¬ëŸ¬ ì´ìƒì˜ í˜„ê¸ˆ ìˆ˜ìµì„ ë°›ê²Œ ë  ê²ƒì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê±°ë˜ëŠ” ì•½ 90ì¼ ë‚´ì— ë§ˆë¬´ë¦¬ë  ì˜ˆì •ì´ë©°, íŒ¨ë°€ë¦¬ ë‹¬ëŸ¬ì˜ ë³¸ì‚¬ëŠ” ì²´ì„œí”¼í¬ì— ê³„ì† ìœ„ì¹˜í•  ê²ƒì…ë‹ˆë‹¤.
In the fourth quarter, our team was focused on achieving three distinct objectives: successfully closing out the year; bringing the strategic review to a favorable conclusion; and setting Dollar Tree on a path to realize its full potential and create long-term value for our associates, customers and shareholders. Dollar Tree offers customers incredible value, convenience and discovery. We finished the year with approximately 2,900 3.0 format stores, including roughly 2,600 conversions and 300 new stores. Before I wrap up the Q4 results, I should note that with the decision to sell Family Dollar, from an accounting perspective, our Dollar Tree and Corporate segments are now reported as continuing operations and Family Dollar results are reported as discontinued operations. Net sales from continuing operations increased 0.7% to $5 billion, reflecting the solid comp performance and strong revenue contribution from noncomp stores, including the former 99 Cents Only portfolio, offset by lapping the 53rd week of last year. Net sales from discontinued operations decreased 11.2% to $3.3 billion, reflecting Family Dollar's 1.3% comp, the impact of store closings and the lapping of last year's 53rd week. Therefore, on a consolidated basis, net sales were $8.3 billion, which was at the high end of our $8.1 billion to $8.3 billion outlook range. I'd like to take a few minutes to talk about tariffs and give you a quick supply chain update. As a large retailer and significant importer, we have years of experience dealing with global trade variability. We intend to remain flexible and nimble, focusing our efforts on sourcing products via channels that deliver the lowest landed cost to us in order to maintain value continuity for our customers. This includes the optionality to shift sourcing to and from different countries within a relatively short time frame. ğŸ“Œ í•µì‹¬ ìš”ì•½

Dollar Tree, Inc. (NASDAQ:DLTR) held its Q4 2024 earnings conference call on March 26, 2025, announcing the sale of its Family Dollar business to Brigade-Macellum for over $1 billion. This strategic move aims to separate the two distinct businesses, allowing each to focus on its specific needs and maximize potential. The sale, expected to close in about 90 days, will result in Dollar Tree receiving over $800 million in cash proceeds. For Q4, Dollar Tree reported a 2% comp growth with a notable increase in traffic and ticket sizes, driven by the multi-price offerings and strong holiday sales. The company also highlighted its efforts to mitigate the impact of tariffs and provided an update on its supply chain strategies, including plans to convert a Family Dollar distribution center in Texas to support Dollar Tree operations. The financial outlook for 2025 anticipates sales between $18.5 billion to $19.1 billion, with an adjusted EPS range of $5 to $5.50, reflecting the transition to operating Dollar Tree as a standalone entity.

During the financial discussion, Michael Creedon of Dollar Tree addressed the company's strategies for mitigating tariffs, which have not been fully included in their guidance. The company has successfully offset 90% of the first round of tariffs and continues to use various strategies such as product specification changes, supplier negotiations, and potential product elimination to manage tariff impacts. Additionally, the introduction of new price points, such as $1.50 and $1.75, is part of their strategy to cope with tariff and inflationary pressures. Creedon expressed confidence in the company's ability to navigate these challenges due to their proactive measures and past experiences with tariffs.

The discussion also touched on the impact of tariffs on financial planning, with a focus on the potential $20 million per month cost if unmitigated. Dollar Tree's approach includes a blend of cost management and strategic pricing adjustments to maintain financial stability. The conversation highlighted the company's ongoing efforts to adapt its business model in response to external economic pressures, ensuring sustained performance and growth.
